    <li> Before reading my review, you will need context:    1. I just received this brush, so my review is based on one day&#x27;s use. I will have to update this review periodically to detail its durability.  2. I only own one comparable brush. It is an off-brand travel-size flat top kabuki that I bought at Marshalls for 10 dollars (it came with a cheapie beauty blender that I tossed.) That brush is also great, so it confirms my suspicions about well-marketed overpriced brushes.    On first impression I am impressed and happy with this brush. It deserves a high rating, but I&#x27;m awarding it 4 stars instead of 5 because of one drawback. As others have mentioned, it has a strong chemical smell, which makes me wonder about the way it was manufactured, and how a smell could linger for so long during its shipping process.    Also: does its chemical smell indicate toxicity? Is this detrimental to use on my face? These are important questions to ask, and merit further investigation.    But for purposes of functionality, I&#x27;ll put the smell factor on hold and focus on the brush&#x27;s functionality.    This brush is immediately excellent. Though it arrived smelling horribly, after a wash the smell subdued.    Pro: The package gives you clear instructions on how to wash the brush. The package is also ziplock like, so you can keep it for travel. (But realistically it&#x27;s not all that functional if you have a brush collection or makeup bag.)    I purchased this brush after doing extensive research for a week on alternatives to the more popular Sigma F80. I had started immersing myself in the makeup world, and all of the Youtube Beauty gurus were recommending the Sigma. However, it&#x27;s hard for me to trust a group that is paid to hawk products. So I went searching alternative brushes.    I also believe, after some research, that many of the branded brushes are manufactured in China or elsewhere by the same companies. So it&#x27;s possible to find replicate products. They just won&#x27;t be branded.    That&#x27;s what this brush is to me. A great product that could be on the market with another brand name on the handle.    Specs:  It is very soft.  It applies both my primer and foundation well.    Questions I have about it:  -How much product gets stuck in the bristles? I once almost purchased the Bare Minerals Perfecting Face Brush, but the sales woman recommended I get a beauty blender instead because the brush is extremely hard to clean. This brush may have similar issues--the foundation may end up getting stuck because the bristles are dense and close together. Not only wrinkles, which is a whole other story, but my pores seemed to have grown to gargantuan size.  I know I had some acne scars from my teenage years but they seemed to have grown much larger with age.  So back to the department store makeup counter I went and picked up a bottle of liquid foundation that promised to give me that dewey look of youth.  The sales woman told me I absolutely needed to use a foundation brush to apply this new foundation [which she would sell me for $36.00] but I thought it kind of weird to use a brush to put my makeup on and politely declined.  [I figured I could just do it the old fashioned way - with my fingers - which cost me nothing.]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I thought applying makeup after getting out of the habit for so many years would be like riding a bike. That $40 bottle of foundation was not hiding those acne scars [so much for the &amp;#34;dewey look&amp;#34;, I thought] and I figured I had just wasted my money on a product that did nothing for my face.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And then I came across this brush, the Premium Foundation Makeup Brush - Flat Top from Beauty Junkees [LOVE that company name!]. With a simple &amp;#34;stippling&amp;#34; and twisting motion I was able to magically fill in those acne scars!  I then used another brush to apply a light coating of powder and my skin actually looked flawless!     <li> I use many types of brushes at different price points - from good ol&#x27; drugstore Revlon (still going strong after many, many years) to spendy Jane Iredale -- as well as faves priced in the middle (RealTechniques and Japonesque).  Almost every brush I have offers value in its own way, as long as I respect just how that particular tool works best.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;BUT-  I&#x27;m pickiest about my foundation brush, as this is what &amp;#34;sets the canvas&amp;#34; for everything else. My current foundation brush, wearing out from repeated, almost daily use over 10 years, is Jane Iredale&#x27;s &amp;#34;The Handi.&amp;#34; Replacing it proves expensive enough that I decided to first shop around --- and man, I&#x27;m glad I did!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Beauty Junkees&#x27; Flat Top Kabuki is hands-down, the best and most versatile brush I have ever used - regardless of price. When I pulled it out of its package, I was blown away because, while hopeful based on other reviews, I was simply not expecting the level of quality.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Heft and balance: perfect. The handle is satisfying to hold, with a very substantial brush head so dense, it doesn&#x27;t splay when you push down hard on it. This is a large brush, but not overly so - I carry it in my makeup bag daily.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Feel: no scratching, it&#x27;s one of the softest brushes I have and feels like teddy bear fur!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Shedding: it doesn&#x27;t. I&#x27;ve used it every day for several weeks and not a hair has come out that I&#x27;ve noticed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Media: works exceptionally for any kind of base (BB cream, creme or lotion foundation - and powdered minerals, which I use most often). Works with setting powders, too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Vegan friendly - yes. ORIGINAL REVIEW: This review is for the Flat Top Kabuki brush. I have used this brush a few times for applying my liquid foundation and am very impressed with the way it applies foundation to my face. Previously, I was using the Real Techniques stippling brush and was quite pleased with the results but once I used this Beauty Junkees, the difference was noticeable. The foundation seemed even more airbrushed, even, and more natural.  The bristles are extraordinarily soft and it is a pleasure to use on my face. I have never used a brush this large for applying foundation so am still getting used to going around my eyes and nose with it (I find it a bit awkward around tight areas--but certainly can not reduce my rating because of my own preferences in brush shapes.)  The only real negative I have about the brush so far is the awful and extremely potent/toxic glue smell that permeated both the inside of the package and on the brush itself when first opening it. The smell was so strong I feared the glue for the bristles was not sufficiently cured. Fortunately, the smell disappeared after washing the brush thoroughly with baby shampoo but now I am a bit wary about the bristles falling out with repeated washing , especially after having to wash it so frequently because of its use with liquid foundations that needs to be removed often. Hopefully, this is not the case but I did deduct a star for this horrible smell.  But, other than the smell, really am liking it so far.</li>
